## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population size P. Classical population dynamics models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor modeling)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy growth-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric growth curve)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with proportional removal)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal environmental variation)
- Density-dependent with time decay: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) * (1 - c2 * P) (time-varying intrinsic rate)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order competition effects)
- Beverton-Holt continuous form: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (rational density dependence)
- Weak Allee logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P**2 * (1 - c1 * P) (cooperative growth at low density)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent exponential phase — multiplicative P factor is fundamental
- Quadratic P term (P² or P*(1-cP)) indicates intraspecific competition or density-dependent regulation
- Logarithmic dependence on P (P*log(c/P)) suggests Gompertz-type asymmetric growth where decline rate slows near carrying capacity
- Cubic terms in P (P*(P-a)*(K-P)) indicate strong Allee effects with bistability and a critical population threshold
- Ratio of powers of P (P^a - P^b with a<b) suggests metabolic scaling models where growth and maintenance scale differently
- Explicit time dependence beyond P suggests non-autonomous dynamics: environmental forcing, seasonality, or resource depletion
- Fractional power of P (P^c with 0<c<1) indicates sub-linear per-capita growth, common in surface-area-limited resource uptake
- Product of P with a saturating function of P (P/(1+cP)) indicates contest competition rather than scramble competition
- Negative constant term independent of P indicates constant-rate harvesting or immigration effects

**GT numerical expression:**
```
0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333
```

Let me expand this step by step.

First term: `0.7214*(-1 + P/6.651)*(1 - P/13.538)*P`

Let me denote a = 6.651, b = 13.538, k = 0.7214 for brevity.

`k*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P = k*(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P`

Expanding `(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)`:
= P/a - P²/(ab) - 1 + P/b

So first term = k*P*(P/a - P²/(ab) - 1 + P/b) = k*(P²/a - P³/(ab) - P + P²/b)

Second term: `k*(1 - P/b)*P = k*(P - P²/b)`

Third term: `k*P^(1/3)`

Combining all:
- P³ coefficient: -k/(ab) = -0.7214/(6.651*13.538) = -0.7214/90.07 ≈ -0.008010
- P² coefficient: k/a + k/b - k/b = k/a = 0.7214/6.651 ≈ 0.10846
- P coefficient: -k + k = 0
- P^(1/3) coefficient: k = 0.7214

So the GT simplifies to:
**GT = c_A * P^(1/3) + c_B * P³ + c_C * P²**

where c_A ≈ 0.7214, c_B ≈ -0.008010, c_C ≈ 0.10846.

Wait, let me double-check the P coefficient. First term gives -k*P, second term gives +k*P. These cancel! And P² terms: k/a + k/b from first term, -k/b from second term = k/a. Yes!

So **GT = 0.7214*P^(1/3) - 0.008010*P³ + 0.10846*P²**

This is exactly the form: `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2`

Now let me check which candidates can match this:

This is exactly the simplified GT form! Set c0 = 0.7214, c1 = -0.008010, c2 = 0.10846.

This is a perfect match.
